				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Exxon_Mobil_Corp.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Exxon Mobil Corp.">Exxon Mobil Corp.</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about Exxon Mobil Corp. For the company's subsidiaries, see <a href="/wiki/Exxon" title="Exxon">Exxon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mobil" title="Mobil">Mobil</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>Exxon Mobil Corporation</b>, <a href="/wiki/Trade_name" title="Trade name">doing business as</a> <b>ExxonMobil</b>, is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_oil_exploration_and_production_companies" title="List of oil exploration and production companies">oil and gas</a> corporation headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Irving,_Texas" title="Irving, Texas">Irving, Texas</a>. It is the largest direct descendant of <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller" title="John D. Rockefeller">John D. Rockefeller</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">Standard Oil</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-exxonmobilhistory_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exxonmobilhistory-2">[2]</a></sup> and was formed on November 30, 1999 by the merger of <a href="/wiki/Exxon" title="Exxon">Exxon</a> (formerly the Standard Oil Company of New Jersey) and <a href="/wiki/Mobil" title="Mobil">Mobil</a> (formerly the Standard Oil Company of New York). ExxonMobil's primary brands are Exxon, Mobil, <a href="/wiki/Esso" title="Esso">Esso</a>, and ExxonMobil Chemical.<sup id="cite_ref-exxonmobilbrands_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exxonmobilbrands-3">[3]</a></sup> ExxonMobil is incorporated in Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" Energy</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Esso" title="Esso">Esso</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Esso_Australia" title="Esso Australia">Esso Australia</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Exxon" title="Exxon">Exxon</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Exxon_Neftegas" title="Exxon Neftegas">Exxon Neftegas</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/FuelCell_Energy" title="FuelCell Energy">FuelCell Energy</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Imperial_Oil" title="Imperial Oil">Imperial Oil</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(69.6%)</span></li><li><a href="/wiki/Mobil" title="Mobil">Mobil</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Mobil_Producing_Nigeria" title="Mobil Producing Nigeria">Mobil Producing Nigeria</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/SeaRiver_Maritime" title="SeaRiver Maritime">SeaRiver Maritime</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Superior_Oil_Company" title="Superior Oil Company">Superior Oil Co.</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Syncrude" title="Syncrude">Syncrude</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(25%)</span></li><li><a href="/wiki/Vacuum_Oil_Company" title="Vacuum Oil Company">Vacuum Oil Co.</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/XTO_Energy" title="XTO Energy">XTO Energy</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://corporate.exxonmobil.com/">corporate<wbr></wbr>.exxonmobil<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table><p><a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_by_revenue" class="mw-redirect" title="List of companies by revenue">One of the world's largest companies by revenue</a>, ExxonMobil from 1996 to 2017 varied from the <a href="/wiki/List_of_corporations_by_market_capitalization" class="mw-redirect" title="List of corporations by market capitalization">first to sixth largest publicly traded company by market capitalization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forbes2000_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes2000-6">[6]</a></sup> The company was ranked ninth globally in the <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Global_2000" title="Forbes Global 2000">Forbes Global 2000</a> list in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> ExxonMobil was the tenth most profitable company in the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> As of 2018, the company ranked second in the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> rankings of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-fortuneglobal500_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortuneglobal500-9">[9]</a></sup> Approximately 55.56% of the company's shares are held by institutions. As of March 2019, ExxonMobil's largest shareholders include <a href="/wiki/The_Vanguard_Group" title="The Vanguard Group">The Vanguard Group</a> (8.15%), <a href="/wiki/BlackRock" title="BlackRock">BlackRock</a> (6.61%), and <a href="/wiki/State_Street_Corporation" title="State Street Corporation">State Street Corporation</a> (4.83%).
</p><p>ExxonMobil is one of the largest of the world's <a href="/wiki/Big_Oil" title="Big Oil">Big Oil</a> companies.<sup id="cite_ref-fortuneglobal500_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortuneglobal500-9">[9]</a></sup> As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it had daily production of 3.921 million BOE (<a href="/wiki/Barrels_of_oil_equivalent" class="mw-redirect" title="Barrels of oil equivalent">barrels of oil equivalent</a>); but significantly smaller than a number of national companies. In 2008, this was approximately 3% of world production, which is less than several of the largest state-owned petroleum companies.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> When ranked by oil and gas reserves, it is 14th in the world—with less than 1% of the total.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> ExxonMobil's reserves were 20 billion BOE at the end of 2016 and the 2007 rates of production were expected to last more than 14 years.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> With 37 <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">oil refineries</a> in 21 countries constituting a combined daily refining capacity of 6.3 million barrels (1,000,000 m<sup>3</sup>), ExxonMobil is the largest refiner in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> a title that was also associated with Standard Oil since its incorporation in 1870.<sup id="cite_ref-exxonmobilhistory_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exxonmobilhistory-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (January 2019)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>ExxonMobil has been criticized for its slow response to cleanup efforts after the 1989 <a href="/wiki/Exxon_Valdez_oil_spill" title="Exxon Valdez oil spill">Exxon Valdez oil spill</a> in Alaska, widely considered to be one of the world's worst oil spills in terms of damage to the environment. ExxonMobil has a history of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels_lobby" title="Fossil fuels lobby">lobbying</a> for <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_denial" title="Climate change denial">climate change denial</a> and against the scientific consensus that <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> is caused by the burning of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>. The company has also been the target of accusations of improperly dealing with human rights issues, influence on <a href="/wiki/American_foreign_policy" class="mw-redirect" title="American foreign policy">American foreign policy</a>, and its impact on the future of nations.<sup id="cite_ref-tel12_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tel12-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none"><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Big_Oil.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Big_Oil.svg/330px-Big_Oil.svg.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="317" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="720"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 330px;height: 317px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Big_Oil.svg/330px-Big_Oil.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="330" data-height="317" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Big_Oil.svg/495px-Big_Oil.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Big_Oil.svg/660px-Big_Oil.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Big_Oil.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chart of the major energy companies dubbed "Big Oil", sorted by latest published revenue</div></div></div>
<p>ExxonMobil was formed in 1999 by the merger of two major oil companies, Exxon and Mobil.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="1870_to_1911">1870 to 1911</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1870 to 1911" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">Standard Oil</a></div>
<p>Both Exxon and Mobil were descendants of <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">Standard Oil</a>, established by <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller" title="John D. Rockefeller">John D. Rockefeller</a> and partners in 1870 as the Standard Oil Company of Ohio. In 1882, it together with its affiliated companies was incorporated as the Standard Oil Trust with Standard Oil Company of New Jersey and Standard Oil Company of New York as its largest companies.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-19">[19]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Anglo-American_Oil_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-American Oil Company">Anglo-American Oil Company</a> was established in the United Kingdom in 1888.<sup id="cite_ref-grace_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grace-20">[20]</a></sup>  In 1890, Standard Oil, together with local ship merchants in Bremen established <i><a href="/wiki/German-American_Petroleum_Society" class="mw-redirect" title="German-American Petroleum Society">Deutsch-Amerikanische Petroleum Gesellschaft</a></i> (later: Esso A.G.).<sup id="cite_ref-britannica-exxon_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-exxon-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-clark_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clark-22">[22]</a></sup>  In 1891, a sale branch for the Netherlands and Belgium, American Petroleum Company, was established in <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-krabbendam_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-krabbendam-23">[23]</a></sup>  At the same year, a sale branch for Italy, <i>Società Italo Americana pel Petrolio</i>, was established in <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-skinner_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-skinner-24">[24]</a></sup></p><p>The Standard Oil Trust was dissolved under the <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Antitrust_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Sherman Antitrust Act">Sherman Antitrust Act</a> in 1892; however, it reemerged as the Standard Oil Interests.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-19">[19]</a></sup>  In 1893, the Chinese and the whole Asian <a href="/wiki/Kerosene" title="Kerosene">kerosene</a> market was assigned to Standard Oil Company of New York in order to improve trade with the Asian counterparts.<sup id="cite_ref-cochran_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cochran-25">[25]</a></sup>  In 1898, Standard Oil of New Jersey acquired controlling stake in <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Oil" title="Imperial Oil">Imperial Oil</a> of Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica-exxon_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-exxon-21">[21]</a></sup>  In 1899, Standard Oil Company of New Jersey became the holding company for the Standard Oil Interests.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-19">[19]</a></sup>  The anti-monopoly proceedings against the Standard Oil were launched in 1898.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-19">[19]</a></sup>  The reputation of Standard Oil in the public eye suffered badly after publication of <a href="/wiki/Ida_M._Tarbell" class="mw-redirect" title="Ida M. Tarbell">Ida M. Tarbell</a>'s classic exposé <i><a href="/wiki/The_History_of_the_Standard_Oil_Company" title="The History of the Standard Oil Company">The History of the Standard Oil Co.</a></i> in 1904, leading to a growing outcry for the government to take action against the company. By 1911, with public outcry at a climax, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a> <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil_Company_of_New_Jersey_v._United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Oil Company of New Jersey v. United States">ruled</a> that Standard Oil must be dissolved and split into 34 companies. Two of these companies were <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil_of_New_Jersey" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Oil of New Jersey">Jersey Standard</a> ("Standard Oil Co. of New Jersey"), which eventually became Exxon, and <a href="/wiki/Socony" class="mw-redirect" title="Socony">Socony</a> ("Standard Oil Co. of New York"), which eventually became Mobil.<sup id="cite_ref-vassiliou_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="1911_to_1950">1911 to 1950</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1911 to 1950" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Over the next few decades, Jersey Standard and Socony grew significantly. John Duston Archbold was the first president of Jersey Standard. Archbold was followed by <a href="/wiki/Walter_C._Teagle" title="Walter C. Teagle">Walter C. Teagle</a> in 1917, who made it the largest oil company in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-vassiliou_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-26">[26]</a></sup>  In 1919, Jersey Standard acquired a 50% share in <a href="/wiki/Humble_Oil" title="Humble Oil">Humble Oil &amp; Refining Co.</a>, a Texas oil producer.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-19">[19]</a></sup>  In 1920, it was listed on the New York Stock Exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-vassiliou_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-26">[26]</a></sup> In the following years it acquired or established Tropical Oil Company of Colombia (1920), Standard Oil Company of Venezuela (1921), and Creole Petroleum Company of Venezuela (1928).<sup id="cite_ref-britannica-exxon_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-exxon-21">[21]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Henry_Clay_Folger" title="Henry Clay Folger">Henry Clay Folger</a> was head of Socony until 1923, when he was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Herbert_L._Pratt" title="Herbert L. Pratt">Herbert L. Pratt</a>. The growing <a href="/wiki/Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile">automotive</a> market inspired the product trademark Mobiloil, registered by Socony in 1920.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>  After dissolution of Standard Oil, Socony had refining and marketing assets but no production activities. For this reason, Socony purchased a 45% interest in <a href="/wiki/Magnolia_Petroleum_Co." class="mw-redirect" title="Magnolia Petroleum Co.">Magnolia Petroleum Co.</a>, a major refiner, marketer and pipeline transporter, in 1918. In 1925, Magnolia became wholly owned by Socony. In 1926, Socony purchased General Petroleum Corporation of California.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_19-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vassiliou_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-26">[26]</a></sup>  In 1928, Socony joined the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Petroleum_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Petroleum Company">Turkish Petroleum Company</a> (Iraq Petroleum Company).<sup id="cite_ref-vassiliou_26-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-26">[26]</a></sup>  In 1931, Socony merged with <a href="/wiki/Vacuum_Oil_Company" title="Vacuum Oil Company">Vacuum Oil Company</a>, an industry pioneer dating back to 1866, to form Socony-Vacuum.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_19-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vassiliou_26-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-time100831_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time100831-27">[27]</a></sup></p><p>In the Asia-Pacific region, Jersey Standard has established through its Dutch subsidiary an exploration and production company <i>Nederlandsche Koloniale Petroleum Maatschappij</i> in 1912. In 1922, it found oil in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and in 1927, it built a refinery in <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-shavit_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shavit-28">[28]</a></sup>  It had oil production and refineries but no marketing network. Socony-Vacuum had Asian marketing outlets supplied remotely from California. In 1933, Jersey Standard and Socony-Vacuum merged their interests in the Asia-Pacific region into a 50–50 joint venture. <a href="/wiki/Standard_Vacuum_Oil_Company" title="Standard Vacuum Oil Company">Standard Vacuum Oil Company</a>, or "Stanvac," operated in 50 countries, from East Africa to New Zealand, before it was dissolved in 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_19-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-19">[19]</a></sup></p><p>In 1924, Jersey Standard and <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> pooled its <a href="/wiki/Tetraethyllead" title="Tetraethyllead">tetraethyllead</a>-related patents and established the <a href="/wiki/Ethyl_Gasoline_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethyl Gasoline Corporation">Ethyl Gasoline Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pound_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pound-29">[29]</a></sup>  In 1927, Jersey Standard signed a 25-years cooperation agreement with <a href="/wiki/IG_Farben" title="IG Farben">IG Farben</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Coal_hydrogenation" class="mw-redirect" title="Coal hydrogenation">coal hydrogenation</a> research in the United States.  Jersey Standard assumed this cooperation to be beneficial as it believed the United States oil reserves to be exhausted in the near future and that the coal hydrogenation would give an access for producing <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_fuel" title="Synthetic fuel">synthetic fuels</a>. It erected synthetic fuel plants in <a href="/wiki/Bayway_Refinery" title="Bayway Refinery">Bayway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge_Refinery" title="Baton Rouge Refinery">Baton Rouge</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Baytown_Refinery" title="Baytown Refinery">Baytown</a> (unfinished). The interest in hydrogenation evaporated after discovery of the <a href="/wiki/East_Texas_Oil_Field" title="East Texas Oil Field">East Texas Oil Field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lesch_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lesch-30">[30]</a></sup>  As a part of the cooperation between Jersey Standard and IG Farben, a joint company, Standard I.G. Company, was established with Jersey Standard having a stake of 80%.  IG Farben transferred rights to the hydrogenation process outside of Germany to the joint venture in exchange of $35 million stake of Jersey Standard shares.<sup id="cite_ref-herbert_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-herbert-31">[31]</a></sup>  In 1930, the joint company established Hydro Patents Company to license the hydrogenation process in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-nowell_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nowell-32">[32]</a></sup>  The agreement with IG Farben gave to Jersey Standard access to patents related to <a href="/wiki/Polyisobutylene" class="mw-redirect" title="Polyisobutylene">polyisobutylene</a> which assist Jersey Standard to advance in isobutolene polymerization and to produce the first <a href="/wiki/Butyl_rubber" title="Butyl rubber">butyl rubber</a> in 1937.<sup id="cite_ref-vassiliou_26-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-butyl_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-butyl-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-morton_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morton-34">[34]</a></sup>  As the agreement with IG Farben gave to the German company a veto right of licensing chemical industry patents in the United States, including patent for butyl rubber, Jersey Standard was accused of treason by senator <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Harry S. Truman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rockoff_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rockoff-35">[35]</a></sup>  In 1941, it opened the first commercial synthetic <a href="/wiki/Toluene" title="Toluene">toluene</a> plant.<sup id="cite_ref-vassiliou_26-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-26">[26]</a></sup></p><p>In 1932, Jersey Standard acquired foreign assets of the <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Petroleum_and_Transport_Company" title="Pan American Petroleum and Transport Company">Pan American Petroleum and Transport Company</a>. In 1937, its assets in Bolivia were nationalized, followed by nationalization of its assets in Mexico in 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-vassiliou_26-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-26">[26]</a></sup></p><p>Since the 1911 Standard Oil Trust breakup, Jersey Standard used the trademark <a href="/wiki/Esso" title="Esso">Esso</a>, a phonetic pronunciation of the initials "S" and "O" in the name Standard Oil,<sup id="cite_ref-exxonmobilhistory_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exxonmobilhistory-2">[2]</a></sup> as one of its primary brand names.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT19721025_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT19721025-36">[36]</a></sup> However, several of the other Standard Oil spinoffs objected to the use of that name in their territories, and successfully got the U.S. federal courts in the 1930s to ban the Esso brand in those states.<sup id="cite_ref-CSP_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSP-37">[37]</a></sup> In those territories where the ban was in force, Jersey Standard instead marketed its products under the <a href="/wiki/Enco_(brand)" title="Enco (brand)">Enco</a> or Humble names.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT19721025_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT19721025-36">[36]</a></sup></p><p>In 1935, Socony Vacuum Oil opened the huge Mammoth Oil Port on <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island" title="Staten Island">Staten Island</a> which had a capacity of handling a quarter of a billion gallons of petroleum products a year and could transship oil from ocean-going tankers and river barges.<sup id="cite_ref-Popular_Mechanics_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Popular_Mechanics-38">[38]</a></sup> In 1940, Socony-Vacuum purchased the Gilmore Oil Company of California, which in 1945 was merged with another subsidiary, General Petroleum Corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-darr_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-darr-39">[39]</a></sup>  In 1947, Jersey Standard and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a> formed the joint venture <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nederlandse_Aardolie_Maatschappij" class="extiw" title="nl:Nederlandse Aardolie Maatschappij">Nederlandse Aardolie Maatschappij BV</a> for oil and gas exploration and production in the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-tjemkes_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tjemkes-40">[40]</a></sup>  In 1948, Jersey Standard and Socony-Vacuum acquired interests in the <a href="/wiki/Arab-American_Oil_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab-American Oil Company">Arab-American Oil Company</a> (Aramco).<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_19-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-green_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-green-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="1950_to_1972">1950 to 1972</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1950 to 1972" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1955, Socony-Vacuum became Socony Mobil Oil Company.  In 1959, Magnolia Petroleum Company, General Petroleum Corporation, and Mobil Producing Company were merged to form the Mobil Oil Company, a <a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">wholly owned subsidiary</a> of Socony Mobil. In 1966, Socony Mobil Oil Company became the Mobil Oil Corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_19-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-19">[19]</a></sup></p><p>Humble Oil became a wholly owned subsidiary of Jersey Standard and was reorganized into the United States marketing division of Jersey Standard in 1959.  In 1967, Humble Oil purchased all remaining Signal stations from <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil_Company_of_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Oil Company of California">Standard Oil Company of California</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron</a>) In 1969, Humble Oil opened a new refinery in <a href="/wiki/Benicia,_California" title="Benicia, California">Benicia, California</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In Libya, Jersey Standard made its first major oil discovery in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_19-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-19">[19]</a></sup></p><p>Mobil Chemical Company was established in 1960 and Exxon Chemical Company (first named Enjay Chemicals) in 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_19-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-19">[19]</a></sup></p><p>In 1965, Jersey Standard started to acquire coal assets through its affiliate Carter Oil (later renamed Exxon Coal, U.S.A.). For managing the Midwest and Eastern coal assets in the United States, the Monterey Coal Company was established in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-chakravarthy_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chakravarthy-42">[42]</a></sup>  Carter Oil focused on the developing synthetic fuels from coal.<sup id="cite_ref-chakravarthy_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chakravarthy-42">[42]</a></sup> In 1966, it started to develop the <a href="/wiki/Coal_liquefaction" title="Coal liquefaction">coal liquefaction</a> process called the <a href="/wiki/Exxon_Donor_Solvent_Process" class="mw-redirect" title="Exxon Donor Solvent Process">Exxon Donor Solvent Process</a>. In April 1980, Exxon opened a 250-ton-per-day pilot plant in <a href="/wiki/Baytown,_Texas" title="Baytown, Texas">Baytown, Texas</a>. The plant was closed and dismantled in 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-kent_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kent-43">[43]</a></sup></p><p>In 1967, Mobil acquired a 28% strategic stake in the German fuel chain <a href="/wiki/Aral_A.G." class="mw-redirect" title="Aral A.G.">Aral</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-weiand_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weiand-44">[44]</a></sup></p><p>In late 1960s Jersey Standard task force was looking for projects 30 years in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-williams_2005_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-williams_2005-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-perlin_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perlin-46">[46]</a></sup> In April 1973, Exxon founded Solar Power Corporation, a wholly owned subsidiary for manufacturing of terrestrial <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_cell" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic cell">photovoltaic cells</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jones_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jones-47">[47]</a></sup>  After <a href="/wiki/1980s_oil_glut" title="1980s oil glut">1980s oil glut</a> Exxon's internal report projected that solar would not become viable until 2012 or 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg041115_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg041115-48">[48]</a></sup>  Consequently, Exxon sold Solar Power Corporation in 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-jones_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jones-47">[47]</a></sup>  In 1974–1994, also Mobil developed solar energy through Mobil Tyco Solar Energy Corporation, its joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Tyco_Laboratories" class="mw-redirect" title="Tyco Laboratories">Tyco Laboratories</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jones_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jones-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-muhlbauer_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-muhlbauer-49">[49]</a></sup></p><p>In late 1960s, Jersey Standard entered into the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear industry">nuclear industry</a>. In 1969, it created a subsidiary, Jersey Nuclear Company (later: Exxon Nuclear Company), for manufacturing and marketing of uranium fuel, which was to be fabricated from uranium concentrates mined by the mineral department of Humble Oil (later: Exxon Minerals Company).<sup id="cite_ref-taylor220883_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taylor220883-50">[50]</a></sup>  In 1970, Jersey Nuclear opened a nuclear fuel manufacturing facility, now owned by <a href="/wiki/Framatome" title="Framatome">Framatome</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Richland,_Washington" title="Richland, Washington">Richland, Washington</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-areva301015_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-areva301015-51">[51]</a></sup>  In 1986, Exxon Nuclear was sold to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kraftwerk_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kraftwerk Union (page does not exist)">Kraftwerk Union</a>, a nuclear arm of <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ferguson_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ferguson-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt241286_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt241286-53">[53]</a></sup> The company started surface mining of uranium ore in <a href="/wiki/Converse_County,_Wyoming" title="Converse County, Wyoming">Converse County, Wyoming</a>, in 1970, solution mining in 1972, and underground mining in 1977. Uranium ore processing started in 1972. The facility was closed in 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-nrc-highlands_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nrc-highlands-54">[54]</a></sup>  In 1973, Exxon acquired the <a href="/wiki/Ray_Point,_Texas" title="Ray Point, Texas">Ray Point</a> uranium ore processing facility which was shortly afterwards decommissioned.<sup id="cite_ref-nrc-texas_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nrc-texas-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="1972_to_1998">1972 to 1998</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1972 to 1998" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1972, Exxon was unveiled as the new, unified brand name for all former Enco and Esso outlets. At the same time, the company changed its corporate name from Standard Oil of New Jersey to Exxon Corporation, and Humble Oil became Exxon Company, U.S.A.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_19-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-19">[19]</a></sup>  The rebranding came after successful test-marketing of the Exxon name, under two experimental logos, in the fall and winter of 1971-72. Along with the new name, Exxon settled on a rectangular logo using red lettering and blue trim on a white background, similar to the familiar color scheme on the old Enco and Esso logos. Exxon replaced the <a href="/wiki/Esso" title="Esso">Esso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enco_(oil_company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Enco (oil company)">Enco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Humble_Oil" title="Humble Oil">Humble</a> brands in the United States on January 1, 1973.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Due to the <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">oil embargo of 1973</a>, Exxon and Mobil began to expand their exploration and production into the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>, Africa and Asia. Mobil diversified its activities into retail sale and packaging by acquiring the parent company of <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_Ward" title="Montgomery Ward">Montgomery Ward</a> and <a href="/wiki/Container_Corporation_of_America" title="Container Corporation of America">Container Corporation of America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_19-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-19">[19]</a></sup></p><p>In 1976, Exxon, through its subsidiary Intercor, entered into partnership with Colombian state owned company Carbocol to start coal mining in <a href="/wiki/Cerrej%C3%B3n" title="Cerrejón">Cerrejón</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cerrejon_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cerrejon-56">[56]</a></sup>  In 1980, Exxon merged its assets in the mineral industry into newly established Exxon Minerals (later ExxonMobil Coal and Minerals).<sup id="cite_ref-obrien_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obrien-57">[57]</a></sup>  At the same year, Exxon entered into the <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale_industry" title="Oil shale industry">oil shale industry</a> by buying a 60% stake in the <a href="/wiki/Colony_Shale_Oil_Project" title="Colony Shale Oil Project">Colony Shale Oil Project</a> in Colorado, United States,<sup id="cite_ref-fu_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fu-58">[58]</a></sup> and 50% stake in the Rundle oil shale deposit in <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>, Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-symington_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-symington-59">[59]</a></sup>  On May 2, 1982, Exxon announced the termination of the Colony Shale Oil Project because of low oil-prices and increased expenses.<sup id="cite_ref-vassiliou_26-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fu_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fu-58">[58]</a></sup></p><p>Mobil moved its headquarters from <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a> to <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">Fairfax County, Virginia</a>, in 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-DawsonExxon2_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DawsonExxon2-60">[60]</a></sup>  Exxon sold the <a href="/wiki/Exxon_Building_(New_York)" class="mw-redirect" title="Exxon Building (New York)">Exxon Building</a> (1251 Avenue of the Americas), its former headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Center" title="Rockefeller Center">Rockefeller Center</a>, to a unit of Mitsui Real Estate Development Co. Ltd. in 1986 for $610 million, and in 1989, moved its headquarters from <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, New York City to the <a href="/wiki/Las_Colinas" title="Las Colinas">Las Colinas</a> area of <a href="/wiki/Irving,_Texas" title="Irving, Texas">Irving, Texas</a>. John Walsh, president of Exxon subsidiary Friendswood Development Company, stated that Exxon left New York because the costs were too high.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p><p>On March 24, 1989, the <a href="/wiki/Exxon_Valdez" title="Exxon Valdez">Exxon Valdez</a> <a href="/wiki/Oil_tanker" title="Oil tanker">oil tanker</a> struck <a href="/wiki/Bligh_Reef" title="Bligh Reef">Bligh Reef</a> in <a href="/wiki/Prince_William_Sound" title="Prince William Sound">Prince William Sound</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> and spilled more than 11 million US gallons (42,000 m<sup>3</sup>) of crude oil. The <a href="/wiki/Exxon_Valdez_oil_spill" title="Exxon Valdez oil spill">Exxon Valdez oil spill</a> was the second largest in U.S. history, and in the aftermath of the Exxon Valdez incident, the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Congress of the United States">U.S. Congress</a> passed the <a href="/wiki/Oil_Pollution_Act_of_1990" title="Oil Pollution Act of 1990">Oil Pollution Act of 1990</a>. An initial award of US$5 billion <a href="/wiki/Punitive_damages" title="Punitive damages">punitive</a> was reduced to $507.5 million by the US Supreme Court in June 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> and distributions of this award have commenced.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In 1994, Mobil established a subsidiary MEGAS (Mobil European Gas) which became responsible for its Mobil's natural gas operations in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-vap101194_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vap101194-63">[63]</a></sup>  In 1996, Mobil and <a href="/wiki/British_Petroleum" class="mw-redirect" title="British Petroleum">British Petroleum</a> merged their European refining and marketing of fuels and lubricants businesses.  Mobil had 30% stake in fuels and 51% stake in lubricants businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-ec070896_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ec070896-64">[64]</a></sup></p><p>In 1996, Exxon entered into the Russian market by signing a production sharing agreement on the <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin-I" title="Sakhalin-I">Sakhalin-I</a> project.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt110696_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt110696-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="1998_to_2000">1998 to 2000</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1998 to 2000" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1998, Exxon and Mobil signed a US$73.7 billion merger agreement forming a new company called Exxon Mobil Corp. (ExxonMobil), the largest oil company and the third largest company in the world. This was the largest corporate merger at that time. At the time of the merge, Exxon was the world's largest energy company while Mobil was the second largest oil and gas company in the United States. The merger announcement followed shortly after the merge of <a href="/wiki/British_Petroleum" class="mw-redirect" title="British Petroleum">British Petroleum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amoco" title="Amoco">Amoco</a>, which was the largest industrial merger at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc021298_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc021298-66">[66]</a></sup>  Formally, Mobil was bought by Exxon. Mobil's shareholders received 1.32 Exxon's share for each Mobil's share. As a result, the former Mobil's shareholders receives about 30% in the merged company while the stake of former Exxon's shareholders was about 70%. The head of Exxon <a href="/wiki/Lee_Raymond" title="Lee Raymond">Lee Raymond</a> remained the chairman and chief executive of the new company and Mobil chief executive Lucio Noto became vice-chairman.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc021298_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc021298-66">[66]</a></sup>  The merger of Exxon and Mobil was unique in <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States" title="History of the United States">American history</a> because it reunited the two largest companies of the Standard Oil trust.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt031298_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt031298-67">[67]</a></sup></p><p>The merger was approved by the European Commission on September 29, 1999, and by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Federal_Trade_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Federal Trade Commission">United States Federal Trade Commission</a> on November 30, 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-ec290999_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ec290999-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wsj011299_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj011299-69">[69]</a></sup>   As a condition for the Exxon and Mobil merger, the European Commission ordered to dissolve the Mobil's partnership with BP, as also to sell its stake in Aral.<sup id="cite_ref-weiand_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weiand-44">[44]</a></sup>  As a result, BP acquired all fuels assets, two <a href="/wiki/Base_oil" title="Base oil">base oil</a> plants, and a substantial part of the joint venture's finished lubricants business, while ExxonMobil acquired other base oil plants and a part of the finished lubricants business.<sup id="cite_ref-ec030200_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ec030200-70">[70]</a></sup>  The stake in Aral was sold to Vega Oel, later acquired by BP.<sup id="cite_ref-weiand_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weiand-44">[44]</a></sup>  The European Commission also demanded divesting of Mobil's MEGAS and Exxon's 25% stake in the German gas transmission company Thyssengas.<sup id="cite_ref-ogj251099_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ogj251099-71">[71]</a></sup>  MEGAS was acquired by <a href="/wiki/Duke_Energy" title="Duke Energy">Duke Energy</a> and the stake in Thyssengas was acquired by RWE.<sup id="cite_ref-dbj030400_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dbj030400-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dbj030400_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dbj030400-72">[72]</a></sup> The company also divested Exxon's aviation fuel business to BP and Mobil's certain pipeline capacity servicing <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rudnick_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rudnick-73">[73]</a></sup>  The Federal Trade Commission required to sell 2,431 gas stations in the Northeast and Mid-Atlantic (1,740), California (360), Texas (319), and <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> (12).  In addition, ExxonMobil should sell its <a href="/wiki/Benicia_Refinery" title="Benicia Refinery">Benicia Refinery</a> in California, terminal operations in Boston, the Washington, D.C. area and Guam, interest in the <a href="/wiki/Colonial_pipeline" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonial pipeline">Colonial pipeline</a>, Mobil's interest in the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Alaska_Pipeline_System" title="Trans-Alaska Pipeline System">Trans-Alaska Pipeline System</a>, Exxon's jet turbine oil business, and give-up the option to buy <a href="/wiki/Tosco_Corporation" title="Tosco Corporation">Tosco Corporation</a> gas stations.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn301199_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn301199-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ftc301199_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ftc301199-75">[75]</a></sup>  The Benicia Refinery and 340 Exxon-branded stations in California were bought by <a href="/wiki/Valero_Energy_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Valero Energy Corporation">Valero Energy Corporation</a> in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-ogj130300_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ogj130300-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2000_to_present">2000 to present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2000 to present" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vice_President_Cheney_Talks_with_Rex_Tillerson_of_Exxon_Mobil_Corporation_in_His_West_Wing_Office.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Vice_President_Cheney_Talks_with_Rex_Tillerson_of_Exxon_Mobil_Corporation_in_His_West_Wing_Office.jpg/220px-Vice_President_Cheney_Talks_with_Rex_Tillerson_of_Exxon_Mobil_Corporation_in_His_West_Wing_Office.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4992" data-file-height="3328"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Vice_President_Cheney_Talks_with_Rex_Tillerson_of_Exxon_Mobil_Corporation_in_His_West_Wing_Office.jpg/220px-Vice_President_Cheney_Talks_with_Rex_Tillerson_of_Exxon_Mobil_Corporation_in_His_West_Wing_Office.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vice_President_Cheney_Talks_with_Rex_Tillerson_of_Exxon_Mobil_Corporation_in_His_West_Wing_Office.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>ExxonMobil Chairman <a href="/wiki/Rex_Tillerson" title="Rex Tillerson">Rex Tillerson</a> with Vice President <a href="/wiki/Dick_Cheney" title="Dick Cheney">Dick Cheney</a>, 2007</div></div></div>
<p>In the late 1990s and early 2000s, ExxonMobil has received a lot of criticism along with <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_National_Petroleum_Corporation" title="China National Petroleum Corporation">China National Petroleum Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lukoil" title="Lukoil">Lukoil</a>, for increasing oil production facilities in the <a href="/wiki/Rumaila_oil_field" title="Rumaila oil field">Rumaila oil field</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Qurna_Field" title="West Qurna Field">West Qurna Field</a> following the Iraqi government's lack of power and instability resulting from the Iraq War. ExxonMobil alone produces 2,325,000 bpd or $967,432,500 per year of gross revenue in Iraq to maintain low prices. This practice is considered to be beneficial to the big oil consumer countries and allows Exxon to produce higher profit crude oil products such as plastic, fertilizer, medication, lubricant, and clothing.
</p><p>In 2002, the company sold its stake in the <a href="/wiki/Cerrej%C3%B3n" title="Cerrejón">Cerrejón</a> coal mine in Colombia, and copper-mining business in Chile.<sup id="cite_ref-cerrejon_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cerrejon-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wsj030502_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj030502-77">[77]</a></sup>  At the same time, it renewed its interest in oil shale by developing the <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil_Electrofrac" title="ExxonMobil Electrofrac">ExxonMobil Electrofrac</a> <i>in-situ</i> extraction process. In 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Land_Management" title="Bureau of Land Management">Bureau of Land Management</a> approved their research and development project in <a href="/wiki/Rio_Blanco_County,_Colorado" title="Rio Blanco County, Colorado">Rio Blanco County, Colorado</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sentinel110314_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sentinel110314-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-oilprice180314_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oilprice180314-79">[79]</a></sup>  However, in November 2015 the company relinquished its federal research, development and demonstration lease.<sup id="cite_ref-gjsentinel270316_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gjsentinel270316-80">[80]</a></sup>  In 2009, ExxonMobil phased-out coal mining by selling its last operational coal mine in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-srj270109_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-srj270109-81">[81]</a></sup></p><p>In 2008, ExxonMobil started to phase-out from the United States direct-served retail market by selling its <a href="/wiki/Filling_station" title="Filling station">service stations</a>. The usage of Exxon and Mobil brands was <a href="/wiki/Franchising" title="Franchising">franchised</a> to the new owners.<sup id="cite_ref-Erman_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Erman-82">[82]</a></sup></p><p>In 2010, ExxonMobil bought <a href="/wiki/XTO_Energy" title="XTO Energy">XTO Energy</a>, the company focused on development and production of unconventional resources.<sup id="cite_ref-upstream2_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upstream2-83">[83]</a></sup></p><p>In 2011, ExxonMobil started a strategic cooperation with Russian oil company <a href="/wiki/Rosneft" title="Rosneft">Rosneft</a> to develop the <a href="/wiki/East-Prinovozemelsky_field" title="East-Prinovozemelsky field">East-Prinovozemelsky field</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Kara_Sea" title="Kara Sea">Kara Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tuapse_field" title="Tuapse field">Tuapse field</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup>  In 2012, ExxonMobil concluded an agreement with Rosneft to assess possibilities to produce <a href="/wiki/Tight_oil" title="Tight oil">tight oil</a> from <a href="/wiki/Bazhenov_Formation" title="Bazhenov Formation">Bazhenov</a> and Achimov formations in <a href="/wiki/Western_Siberia" title="Western Siberia">Western Siberia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj150612_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj150612-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> In 2018, due to <a href="/wiki/International_sanctions_during_the_Ukrainian_crisis" title="International sanctions during the Ukrainian crisis">international sanctions imposed against Russia and Rosneft</a>, ExxonMobil announces that it will end these joint ventures with Rosneft, but will continue the Sakhalin-I project.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The company estimates it would cost about $200 million after tax.<sup id="cite_ref-ft010318_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft010318-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reuters280218_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters280218-89">[89]</a></sup></p><p>In 2012, ExxonMobil started a <a href="/wiki/Coalbed_methane" title="Coalbed methane">coalbed methane</a> development in Australia, but withdrew from the project in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-australian171214_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-australian171214-90">[90]</a></sup></p><p>In 2012, ExxonMobil confirmed a deal for production and exploration activities in the Kurdistan region of Iraq.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p><p>In November 2013, ExxonMobil agreed to sell its majority stakes in a <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>-based utility and power storage firm, Castle Peak Co Ltd, for a total of $3.4 billion, to <a href="/wiki/CLP_Holdings" class="mw-redirect" title="CLP Holdings">CLP Holdings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p><p>In 2014, ExxonMobil had two "non-monetary" asset swap deals with LINN Energy LLC. In these transactions, ExxonMobil gave to LINN interests in the <a href="/wiki/South_Belridge_Oil_Field" title="South Belridge Oil Field">South Belridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hugoton_Gas_Field" title="Hugoton Gas Field">Hugoton</a> gas fields in the exchange of assets in the <a href="/wiki/Permian_Basin_(North_America)" title="Permian Basin (North America)">Permian Basin</a> in Texas and the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Basin" title="Delaware Basin">Delaware Basin</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ogj190914_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ogj190914-93">[93]</a></sup></p><p>On October 9, 2014, the <a href="/wiki/International_Centre_for_Settlement_of_Investment_Disputes" title="International Centre for Settlement of Investment Disputes">International Centre for Settlement of Investment Disputes</a> awarded ExxonMobil $1.6 billion in the case the company had brought against the Venezuelan government. ExxonMobil alleged that the Venezuelan government illegally expropriated its Venezuelan assets in 2007 and paid unfair compensation.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Securities and Exchange Commission">Securities and Exchange Commission</a> contacted ExxonMobil, questioning why (unlike some other companies<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup>) they had not yet started <a href="/wiki/Write-down" class="mw-redirect" title="Write-down">writing down</a> the value of their <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil reserve">oil reserves</a>, given that much may have to remain in the ground to comply with future <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_legislation" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate change legislation">climate change legislation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mark_Carney" title="Mark Carney">Mark Carney</a> has expressed concerns about the industry's "<a href="/wiki/Stranded_asset" title="Stranded asset">stranded assets</a>". In October 2016, ExxonMobil conceded it may need to declare a lower value for its in-ground oil, and that it might write down about one-fifth of its reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p><p>Also in September 2016, ExxonMobil successfully asked a U.S. federal court to lift the trademark injunction that banned it from using the Esso brand in various U.S. states. By this time, as a result of numerous mergers and rebranding, the remaining Standard Oil companies that previously objected to the Esso name had been acquired by <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a>. ExxonMobil cited trademark surveys in which there was no longer possible confusion with the Esso name as it was more than seven decades before. BP also had no objection to lifting the ban.<sup id="cite_ref-CSP_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSP-37">[37]</a></sup> ExxonMobil did not specify whether they would now open new stations in the U.S. under the Esso name; they were primarily concerned about the additional expenses of having separate marketing, letterheads, packaging, and other materials that omit "Esso".<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p><p>On December 13, 2016, the CEO of ExxonMobil, <a href="/wiki/Rex_Tillerson" title="Rex Tillerson">Rex Tillerson</a>, was nominated as <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a> by <a href="/wiki/President-elect_of_the_United_States" title="President-elect of the United States">President-elect</a> <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2017, Federal climate investigations of ExxonMobil were considered less likely under the new <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Donald_Trump" title="Presidency of Donald Trump">Trump administration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p><p>On January 9, 2017, it was revealed that <a href="/wiki/Infineum" title="Infineum">Infineum</a>, a joint venture of ExxonMobil and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a> headquartered in England, conducted business with Iran, Syria, and Sudan while those states were under US sanctions. ExxonMobil representatives said that because Infineum was based in Europe and the transactions did not involve any U.S. employees, this did not violate the sanctions.<sup id="cite_ref-exxoniran_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exxoniran-106">[106]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2017, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>'s administration denied a request from ExxonMobil to allow it to resume <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Russia" title="Petroleum industry in Russia">oil drilling in Russia</a>. Representative <a href="/wiki/Adam_Schiff" title="Adam Schiff">Adam Schiff</a> (D-California) said that the "Treasury Department should reject any waiver from sanctions which would allow Exxon Mobile or any other company to resume business with prohibited Russian entities."<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2017, ExxonMobil filed a lawsuit against the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Donald_Trump" title="Cabinet of Donald Trump">Trump administration</a> challenging the finding that the company violated sanctions imposed on Russia. William Holbrook, a company spokesman, said that the ExxonMobil had followed "clear guidance from the White House and Treasury Department when its representatives signed [in May 2014] documents involving ongoing oil and gas activities in Russia with Rosneft".<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2019, following Washington D.C.'s increased sanctions on Iran, a rocket landed near residential headquarters of ExxonMobil, Royal Dutch Shell, and ENI SpA. It came after two separate attacks on United States Military bases in Iraq and one week after a two oil tankers being hit by a 'flying object' in the Gulf of Oman. The U.S. Navy's investigation has led to reasonable suspicion to believe <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>'s connection to the attacks.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Operations" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22ExxonMobil%22">"ExxonMobil"</a> – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22ExxonMobil%22+-wikipedia">news</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22ExxonMobil%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22ExxonMobil%22+-wikipedia">books</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22ExxonMobil%22">scholar</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22ExxonMobil%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p>ExxonMobil is the largest non-government owned company in the energy industry and produces about 3% of the world's oil and about 2% of the world's energy.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p><p>ExxonMobil is organized functionally into a number of global operating divisions. These divisions are grouped into three categories for reference purposes, though the company also has several ancillary divisions, such as Coal &amp; Minerals, which are stand alone. It also owns hundreds of smaller subsidiaries such as <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Oil" title="Imperial Oil">Imperial Oil Limited</a> (69.6% ownership) in Canada, and <a href="/wiki/SeaRiver_Maritime" title="SeaRiver Maritime">SeaRiver Maritime</a>, a petroleum shipping company.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Upstream_(petroleum_industry)" title="Upstream (petroleum industry)">Upstream</a> (oil exploration, extraction, shipping, and wholesale operations) based in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, Texas</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Downstream_(petroleum_industry)" title="Downstream (petroleum industry)">Downstream</a> (marketing, refining, and retail operations) based in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a></li>
<li>Chemical division based in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, Texas</li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Upstream">Upstream</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Upstream" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2017</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p>The upstream division makes up the majority of ExxonMobil's revenue, accounting for approximately 70% of the total.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> In 2014, the company had 25.3 billion barrels (4.02<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>9</sup> m<sup>3</sup>) of oil-equivalent reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters230215_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters230215-112">[112]</a></sup>  In 2013, its reserves replacement ratio was 103%.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters230215_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters230215-112">[112]</a></sup></p><p>In the United States, ExxonMobil's petroleum exploration and production activities are concentrated in the <a href="/wiki/Permian_Basin_(North_America)" title="Permian Basin (North America)">Permian Basin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bakken_Formation" title="Bakken Formation">Bakken Formation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woodford_Shale" class="mw-redirect" title="Woodford Shale">Woodford Shale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caney_Shale" class="mw-redirect" title="Caney Shale">Caney Shale</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>. In addition, ExxonMobil has several gas developments in the regions of <a href="/wiki/Marcellus_Shale" class="mw-redirect" title="Marcellus Shale">Marcellus Shale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utica_Shale" title="Utica Shale">Utica Shale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haynesville_Shale" title="Haynesville Shale">Haynesville Shale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barnett_Shale" title="Barnett Shale">Barnett Shale</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fayetteville_Shale" title="Fayetteville Shale">Fayetteville Shale</a>. All natural gas activities are conducted by its subsidiary, XTO Energy.  As of December 31, 2014, ExxonMobil owned 14.6 million acres (59,000 km<sup>2</sup>) in the United States, of which 1.7 million acres (6,900 km<sup>2</sup>) were offshore, 1.5 million acres (6,100 km<sup>2</sup>) of which were in the Gulf of Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters-XOM_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-XOM-113">[113]</a></sup>  In California, it has a joint venture called <a href="/wiki/Aera_Energy_LLC" class="mw-redirect" title="Aera Energy LLC">Aera Energy LLC</a> with <a href="/wiki/Shell_Oil_Company" title="Shell Oil Company">Shell Oil</a>. In Canada, the company holds 5.4 million acres (22,000 km<sup>2</sup>), including 1 million acres (4,000 km<sup>2</sup>) offshore and 0.7 million acres (2,800 km<sup>2</sup>) of the <a href="/wiki/Kearl_Oil_Sands_Project" title="Kearl Oil Sands Project">Kearl Oil Sands Project</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters-XOM_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-XOM-113">[113]</a></sup></p><p>In Argentina, ExxonMobil holds 0.9 million acres (3,600 km<sup>2</sup>), Germany 4.9 million acres (20,000 km<sup>2</sup>), in the Netherlands ExxonMobil owns 1.5 million acres (6,100 km<sup>2</sup>), in Norway it owns 0.4 million acres (1,600 km<sup>2</sup>) offshore, and the United Kingdom 0.6 million acres (2,400 km<sup>2</sup>) offshore. In Africa, upstream operations are concentrated in Angola where it owns 0.4 million acres (1,600 km<sup>2</sup>) offshore, Chad where it owns 46,000 acres (19,000 ha), Equatorial Guinea where it owns 0.1 million acres (400 km<sup>2</sup>) offshore, and Nigeria where it owns 0.8 million acres (3,200 km<sup>2</sup>) offshore.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters-XOM_113-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-XOM-113">[113]</a></sup>  In addition, Exxon Mobil plans to start exploration activities off the coast of Liberia and the Ivory Coast.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters131115_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters131115-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reuters171214_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters171214-115">[115]</a></sup>  In the past, ExxonMobil had exploration activities in Madagascar, however these operations were ended due to unsatisfactory results.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters040715_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters040715-116">[116]</a></sup></p><p>In Asia, it holds 9,000 acres (3,600 ha) in Azerbaijan, 1.7 million acres (6,900 km<sup>2</sup>) in Indonesia, of which 1.3 million acres (5,300 km<sup>2</sup>) are offshore, 0.7 million acres (2,800 km<sup>2</sup>) in Iraq, 0.3 million acres (1,200 km<sup>2</sup>) in Kazakhstan, 0.2 million acres (810 km<sup>2</sup>) in Malaysia, 65,000 acres (26,000 ha) in Qatar, 10,000 acres (4,000 ha) in Yemen, 21,000 acres (8,500 ha) in Thailand, and 81,000 acres (33,000 ha) in the United Arab Emirates.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters-XOM_113-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-XOM-113">[113]</a></sup></p><p>In Russia, ExxonMobil holds 85,000 acres (34,000 ha) in the <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin-I" title="Sakhalin-I">Sakhalin-I</a> project. Together with <a href="/wiki/Rosneft" title="Rosneft">Rosneft</a>, it has developed 63.6 million acres (257,000 km<sup>2</sup>) in Russia, including the <a href="/wiki/East-Prinovozemelsky_field" title="East-Prinovozemelsky field">East-Prinovozemelsky field</a>. In Australia, ExxonMobil held 1.7 million acres (6,900 km<sup>2</sup>), including 1.6 million acres (6,500 km<sup>2</sup>) offshore. It also operates the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Longford_Gas_Conditioning_Plant&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Longford Gas Conditioning Plant (page does not exist)">Longford Gas Conditioning Plant</a>, and participates in the development of <a href="/wiki/Gorgon_LNG" class="mw-redirect" title="Gorgon LNG">Gorgon LNG</a> project. In Papua New Guinea, it holds 1.1 million acres (4,500 km<sup>2</sup>), including the <a href="/wiki/PNG_Gas" title="PNG Gas">PNG Gas</a> project.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters-XOM_113-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-XOM-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Midstream">Midstream</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Midstream" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>As of 2019, the company has joint ventures with pipelines to transport its upstream production, such as the Wink to Webster pipeline and the Double E pipeline (for which it has the option to purchase 50%<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>) to transport <a href="/wiki/Permian_Basin_(North_America)" title="Permian Basin (North America)">Permian Basin</a> oil.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Downstream">Downstream</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Downstream" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>ExxonMobil markets products around the world under the brands of <a href="/wiki/Exxon" title="Exxon">Exxon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mobil" title="Mobil">Mobil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Esso" title="Esso">Esso</a>. Mobil is ExxonMobil's primary retail gasoline brand in California, Florida, New York, New England, the Great Lakes and the Midwest. Exxon is the primary brand in the rest of the United States, with the highest concentration of retail outlets located in New Jersey, Pennsylvania, Texas and in the Mid-Atlantic and Southeastern states. Esso is ExxonMobil's primary gasoline brand worldwide except in Australia and New Zealand, where the Mobil brand is used exclusively. In Colombia, both the Esso and Mobil brands are used.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In Japan, ExxonMobil has a 22% stake in TonenGeneral Sekiyu K.K., a refining company.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Chemicals">Chemicals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Chemicals" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>ExxonMobil Chemical is a petrochemical company which was created by merging Exxon's and Mobil's chemical industries.  Its principal products includes basic <a href="/wiki/Olefin" class="mw-redirect" title="Olefin">olefins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aromatic" class="mw-redirect" title="Aromatic">aromatics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethylene_glycol" title="Ethylene glycol">ethylene glycol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polyethylene" title="Polyethylene">polyethylene</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Polypropylene" title="Polypropylene">polypropylene</a> along with speciality lines such as <a href="/wiki/Elastomer" title="Elastomer">elastomers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plasticizer" title="Plasticizer">plasticizers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solvent" title="Solvent">solvents</a>, process fluids, <a href="/wiki/Oxo_alcohol" title="Oxo alcohol">oxo alcohols</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adhesive" title="Adhesive">adhesive</a> <a href="/wiki/Resin" title="Resin">resins</a>. The company also produces synthetic lubricant base stocks as well as lubricant additives, <a href="/wiki/Propylene" class="mw-redirect" title="Propylene">propylene</a> packaging films and <a href="/wiki/Catalysis" title="Catalysis">catalysts</a>. The company was an industry leader in <a href="/wiki/Metallocene_catalyst" class="mw-redirect" title="Metallocene catalyst">metallocene catalyst</a> technology to make unique polymers with improved performance.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> ExxonMobil is the largest producer of butyl rubber.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p><p>Infineum, a joint venture with Royal Dutch Shell, is manufacturing and marketing <a href="/wiki/Crankcase" title="Crankcase">crankcase</a> lubricant additives, <a href="/wiki/Fuel_additive" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuel additive">fuel additives</a>, and specialty lubricant additives, as well as <a href="/wiki/Automatic_transmission_fluid" title="Automatic transmission fluid">automatic transmission fluids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gear_oil" title="Gear oil">gear oils</a>, and industrial oils.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Clean_technology_research">Clean technology research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Clean technology research" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>ExxonMobil conducts research on clean energy technologies, including <a href="/wiki/Algae_fuel" title="Algae fuel">algae biofuels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">biodiesel</a> made from agricultural waste, carbonate <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">fuel cells</a>, and refining crude oil into plastic by using a <a href="/wiki/Membrane" title="Membrane">membrane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Osmosis" title="Osmosis">osmosis</a> instead of heat.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg031117_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg031117-123">[123]</a></sup>  However, it is unlikely the company will commercialize these projects before 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg031117_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg031117-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_data">Financial data</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Financial data" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Fortune Global 500</a>, ExxonMobil was the second largest company, second largest <a href="/wiki/Publicly_held_corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Publicly held corporation">publicly held corporation</a>, and the largest oil company in the United States by 2017 revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-fortuneglobal500_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortuneglobal500-9">[9]</a></sup> For the fiscal year 2017, ExxonMobil reported earnings of US$19.7 billion, with an annual revenue of US$244.363 billion, an increase of 17.4% over the previous fiscal cycle.
</p>
