</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters_and_offices">Headquarters and offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Headquarters and offices" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ExxonMobilDowntownHoustonTX.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/ExxonMobilDowntownHoustonTX.JPG/220px-ExxonMobilDowntownHoustonTX.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/ExxonMobilDowntownHoustonTX.JPG/220px-ExxonMobilDowntownHoustonTX.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ExxonMobilDowntownHoustonTX.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil_Building" title="ExxonMobil Building">ExxonMobil Building</a>. Former ExxonMobil offices in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Houston" title="Downtown Houston">Downtown Houston</a> were vacated in early 2015.</div></div></div>
<p>ExxonMobil's headquarters are located in <a href="/wiki/Irving,_Texas" title="Irving, Texas">Irving, Texas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p><p>As of May 2015, the company was nearing completion of its new campus located in a northern <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> suburb of <a href="/wiki/Spring,_Texas" title="Spring, Texas">Spring</a>, at the intersection of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_45" title="Interstate 45">Interstate 45</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hardy_Toll_Road" title="Hardy Toll Road">Hardy Toll Road</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Parkway" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Parkway">Grand Parkway</a> northern extension. It is an elaborate corporate campus, including twenty office buildings totaling 3,000,000 square feet (280,000 m<sup>2</sup>), a wellness center, laboratory, and three parking garages.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> It is designed to house nearly 10,000 employees with an additional 1,500 employees located in a satellite campus in Hughes Landing in <a href="/wiki/The_Woodlands,_Texas" title="The Woodlands, Texas">The Woodlands, Texas</a>. In October 2010, the company stated that it would not move its headquarters to <a href="/wiki/Greater_Houston" title="Greater Houston">Greater Houston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Board_of_directors">Board of directors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Board of directors" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The current chairman of the board and CEO of Exxon Mobil Corp. is Darren W. Woods. Woods was elected chairman of the board and CEO effective January 1, 2017 after the retirement of former chairman and CEO Rex Tillerson. Before his election as chairman and CEO, Woods was elected president of ExxonMobil and a member of the board of directors in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Exxon-Mobil-Corporation-Dec-2016-8-K_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Exxon-Mobil-Corporation-Dec-2016-8-K-136">[136]</a></sup></p><p>As of February 6, 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the current ExxonMobil board members are:<sup id="cite_ref-BoardofDirector_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BoardofDirector-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Susan_Avery" title="Susan Avery">Susan Avery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woods_Hole_Oceanographic_Institution" title="Woods Hole Oceanographic Institution">Woods Hole Oceanographic Institution</a> president emerita</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Angela_Braly" title="Angela Braly">Angela Braly</a>, former president and CEO of WellPoint (now <a href="/wiki/Anthem_(company)" title="Anthem (company)">Anthem</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ursula_Burns" title="Ursula Burns">Ursula Burns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xerox" title="Xerox">Xerox</a> former chairman and CEO</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Frazier" title="Kenneth Frazier">Kenneth Frazier</a>, chairman of the board, president and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Merck_%26_Co." title="Merck &amp; Co.">Merck &amp; Co.</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Hooley" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Hooley">Joseph Hooley</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Steven_A._Kandarian" title="Steven A. Kandarian">Steven A. Kandarian</a>, chairman, president and CEO of <a href="/wiki/MetLife" title="MetLife">MetLife, Inc.</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Douglas_R._Oberhelman" title="Douglas R. Oberhelman">Douglas R. Oberhelman</a>, former chairman of the board and chief executive officer of <a href="/wiki/Caterpillar_Inc." title="Caterpillar Inc.">Caterpillar Inc.</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Samuel_J._Palmisano" title="Samuel J. Palmisano">Samuel J. Palmisano</a>, former chairman of the board and CEO of <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Steven_Reinemund" title="Steven Reinemund">Steven Reinemund</a>, executive in residence of <a href="/wiki/Wake_Forest_University" title="Wake Forest University">Wake Forest University</a>, retired executive chairman of the board, <a href="/wiki/PepsiCo" title="PepsiCo">PepsiCo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/William_C._Weldon" title="William C. Weldon">William C. Weldon</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Johnson_%26_Johnson" title="Johnson &amp; Johnson">Johnson &amp; Johnson</a> chairman of the board and CEO</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Darren_W._Woods" class="mw-redirect" title="Darren W. Woods">Darren W. Woods</a>, chairman of the board and CEO, ExxonMobil Corporation</li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Management_committee">Management committee</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Management committee" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The current members of ExxonMobil management committee as of February 6, 2019, are:<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li>Darren W. Woods, chairman and CEO</li>
<li>Neil A. Chapman, senior vice president</li>
<li>Andrew P. Swiger, senior vice president and principal financial officer</li>
<li>Jack P. Williams, senior vice president</li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Environmental record" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<p>ExxonMobil's environmental record <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil_climate_change_controversy" title="ExxonMobil climate change controversy">has faced much criticism</a> for its stance and impact on global warming.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> In 2018, the <a href="/wiki/Political_Economy_Research_Institute" title="Political Economy Research Institute">Political Economy Research Institute</a> ranks ExxonMobil tenth among American corporations emitting <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution_in_the_United_States" title="Air pollution in the United States">airborne pollutants</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-toxicindex-air_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-toxicindex-air-140">[140]</a></sup> thirteenth by emitting <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions_by_the_United_States" title="Greenhouse gas emissions by the United States">greenhouse gases</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-toxicindex-ghg_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-toxicindex-ghg-141">[141]</a></sup> and sixteenth by emitting <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution_in_the_United_States" title="Water pollution in the United States">water pollutants</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-toxicindex-water_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-toxicindex-water-142">[142]</a></sup> As of 2005<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, ExxonMobil had committed less than 1% of their profits towards researching alternative energy,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> which, according to the <a href="/wiki/Advocacy_organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Advocacy organization">advocacy organization</a> <a href="/wiki/Ceres_(organization)" title="Ceres (organization)">Ceres</a>, is less than other leading oil companies.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (December 2018)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">Climate change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Climate change" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p><span id="Funding_of_global_warming_disinformation_and_denial"></span>
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil_climate_change_controversy" title="ExxonMobil climate change controversy">ExxonMobil climate change controversy</a></div>
<p>From the late 1970s through the 1980s, Exxon funded research broadly in line with the developing public scientific approach.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes20151009_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes20151009-145">[145]</a></sup> After the 1980s, Exxon curtailed its own climate research and was a leader in <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_denial" title="Climate change denial">climate change denial</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-icn20150921_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icn20150921-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian20070209_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian20070209-148">[148]</a></sup> In 2014, ExxonMobil publicly acknowledged climate change risk.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup>  It nominally supports a <a href="/wiki/Carbon_tax" title="Carbon tax">carbon tax</a>, though that support is weak.<sup id="cite_ref-icn311215_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icn311215-150">[150]</a></sup></p><p>ExxonMobil funded organizations opposed to the <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a> and seeking to influence public opinion about the scientific consensus that <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> is caused by the burning of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian20070209_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian20070209-148">[148]</a></sup> ExxonMobil helped to found and lead the <a href="/wiki/Global_Climate_Coalition" title="Global Climate Coalition">Global Climate Coalition</a>, which opposed greenhouse gas emission regulation.<sup id="cite_ref-icn20150921_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icn20150921-146">[146]</a></sup> In 2007 the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Concerned_Scientists" title="Union of Concerned Scientists">Union of Concerned Scientists</a> said that ExxonMobil granted $16 million, between 1998 and 2005, towards 43 advocacy organizations which dispute the impact of global warming, and that ExxonMobil used disinformation tactics similar to those used by the <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_industry" title="Tobacco industry">tobacco industry</a> in its denials of the link between lung cancer and smoking, saying that the company used many of the same organizations and personnel to cloud the scientific understanding of climate change and delay action on the issue.<sup id="cite_ref-ucs200702_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ucs200702-151">[151]</a></sup></p><p>In 2015, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Attorney_General" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Attorney General">New York Attorney General</a> launched an investigation whether ExxonMobil's statements to investors were consistent with the company's decades of extensive scientific research.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt20151105_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt20151105-152">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> In October 2018, based on this investigation, ExxonMobil was sued by the State of New York, which claimed the company defrauded shareholders by downplaying the risks of climate change for its businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-Times_10-24-18_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times_10-24-18-154">[154]</a></sup> On March 29, 2016, the attorneys general of Massachusetts and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a> announced investigations. Seventeen attorney generals were cooperating on investigations.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup>  In June, the attorneys general of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a> withdrew the subpoena.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters300616_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters300616-158">[158]</a></sup> In December 2019, the New York Supreme Court issued a ruling in favor of Exxon Mobil Corporation. The ruling was written by New York Supreme Court Justice Barry Ostrager, who concluded that AG's office “failed to prove, by a preponderance of the evidence, that ExxonMobil made any material misstatements or omissions about its practices and procedures that misled any reasonable investor”.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p><p>In 2019, InfluenceMap reported that ExxonMobil was among five major oil companies who were collectively spending $195M per year lobbying to block climate change policies.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Sakhalin-I">Sakhalin-I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sakhalin-I" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin-I" title="Sakhalin-I">Sakhalin-I</a></div>
<p>Scientists and environmental groups have voiced concern that the Sakhalin-I oil and gas project in the Russian Far East, operated by an ExxonMobil subsidiary Exxon Neftegas, threatens the critically endangered western <a href="/wiki/Gray_whale" title="Gray whale">gray whale</a> population.<sup id="cite_ref-wwf240409_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wwf240409-161">[161]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup>  Particular concerns were caused by the decision to construct a pier and to start shipping in Piltun Lagoon.<sup id="cite_ref-ens110716_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ens110716-163">[163]</a></sup> ExxonMobil has responded that since 1997 the company has invested over $40 million to the western whale monitoring program.<sup id="cite_ref-phys040916_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phys040916-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Jersey_settlement">New Jersey settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: New Jersey settlement" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil-New_Jersey_environmental_contamination_settlement" title="ExxonMobil-New Jersey environmental contamination settlement">ExxonMobil-New Jersey environmental contamination settlement</a></div>
<p>In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Department_of_Environmental_Protection" title="New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection">New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection</a> sued ExxonMobil for $8.9 billion for lost wetland resources at <a href="/wiki/Constable_Hook" title="Constable Hook">Constable Hook</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bayonne,_New_Jersey" title="Bayonne, New Jersey">Bayonne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bayway_Refinery" title="Bayway Refinery">Bayway Refinery</a> in <a href="/wiki/Linden,_New_Jersey" title="Linden, New Jersey">Linden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NJDEP_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NJDEP-165">[165]</a></sup> Although a <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Superior_Court" title="New Jersey Superior Court">New Jersey Superior Court</a> justice was believed to be close to a ruling, the <a href="/wiki/Governorship_of_Chris_Christie" title="Governorship of Chris Christie">Christie Administration</a> repeatedly asked the judge to wait, since they were reaching a settlement with ExxonMobil's attorneys.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-166">[166]</a></sup>  On Friday, February 19, 2015, lawyers for the Christie administration informed the judge that a deal had been reached. Details of the $225 million settlement - roughly 3% of what the state originally sought - were not immediately released. <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Porrino" title="Christopher Porrino">Christopher Porrino</a> served as Chief Counsel to the <a href="/wiki/Governorship_of_Chris_Christie" title="Governorship of Chris Christie">Christie administration</a> from January 2014 through July 2015 and handled negotiations in the case.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT030515_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT030515-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Human rights" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Accusations_of_ExxonMobil_human_rights_violations_in_Indonesia" title="Accusations of ExxonMobil human rights violations in Indonesia">Accusations of ExxonMobil human rights violations in Indonesia</a></div>
<p>ExxonMobil is the target of human rights activists for actions taken by the corporation in the <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> territory of <a href="/wiki/Aceh" title="Aceh">Aceh</a>. In June 2001, a lawsuit against ExxonMobil was filed in the Federal <a href="/wiki/United_States_district_court" title="United States district court">District Court</a> of <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">the District of Columbia</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Alien_Tort_Claims_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Alien Tort Claims Act">Alien Tort Claims Act</a>. The suit alleges that the ExxonMobil knowingly assisted human rights violations, including <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a>, murder and rape, by employing and providing material support to <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Indonesia">Indonesian military</a> forces, who committed the alleged offenses during <a href="/wiki/Civil_disorder" title="Civil disorder">civil unrest</a> in Aceh. Human rights complaints involving Exxon's (Exxon and Mobil had not yet merged) relationship with the Indonesian military first arose in 1992; the company denies these accusations and filed a <a href="/wiki/Motion_(legal)" title="Motion (legal)">motion to dismiss</a> the suit, which was denied in 2008 by a federal judge.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> But another federal judge dismissed the lawsuit in August 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> The plaintiffs are currently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (May 2015)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> appealing the dismissal.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> ExxonMobil was ranked as the 12th best of 92 oil, gas, and mining companies on indigenous rights in its Arctic operations.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Geopolitical_influence">Geopolitical influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Geopolitical influence" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<p>A July 2012 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">Daily Telegraph</a></i> review of <a href="/wiki/Steve_Coll" title="Steve Coll">Steve Coll</a>'s book, <i>Private Empire: ExxonMobil and American Power</i>, says that he thinks that ExxonMobil is "able to determine American foreign policy and the fate of entire nations".<sup id="cite_ref-tel12_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tel12-17">[17]</a></sup> ExxonMobil increasingly drills in terrains leased to them by <a href="/wiki/Dictatorships" class="mw-redirect" title="Dictatorships">dictatorships</a>, such as those in <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tel12_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tel12-17">[17]</a></sup> Steve Coll describes <a href="/wiki/Lee_Raymond" title="Lee Raymond">Lee Raymond</a>, the corporation's chief executive until 2005, as "notoriously skeptical about climate change and disliked government interference at any level".<sup id="cite_ref-tel12_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tel12-17">[17]</a></sup></p><p>The book was also reviewed in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i>, according to which "ExxonMobil is easy to caricature, and many critics have done so.... It is to Steve Coll's credit that <i>Private Empire</i>, his new book about ExxonMobil, refuses to subscribe to such a simplistic view."  The review describes the company's power in dealing with the countries in which it drills as "constrained".  It notes that the company shut down its operations in Indonesia to distance itself from the abuses committed against the population by that country's army, and that it decided to drill in Chad only after the World Bank agreed to ensure that the oil royalties were used for the population's benefit.  The review closes by noting that "A world addicted to ExxonMobil's product needs to look in the mirror before being too critical of how relentlessly the company supplies it."<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup></p><p>In 1937, <a href="/wiki/Iraq_Petroleum_Company" title="Iraq Petroleum Company">Iraq Petroleum Company</a> (IPC), 23.75 percent owned by Near East Development Corporation (Later renamed ExxonMobil),<sup id="cite_ref-RLA_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RLA-173">[173]</a></sup> signed an oil concession agreement with the Sultan of Muscat. IPC offered financial support to raise an armed force that would assist the Sultan in occupying the interior region of Oman, an area that geologists believed to be rich in oil. This led to the 1954 outbreak of <a href="/wiki/Jebel_Akhdar_War" title="Jebel Akhdar War">Jebel Akhdar War</a> in Oman that lasted for more than 5 years.<sup id="cite_ref-OmansInsurgencies_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OmansInsurgencies-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-globalsecurity_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalsecurity-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents">Accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Accidents" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Exxon_Valdez_oil_spill">Exxon Valdez oil spill</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Exxon Valdez oil spill" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Exxon_Valdez_oil_spill" title="Exxon Valdez oil spill">Exxon Valdez oil spill</a></div>
<p>The March 24, 1989, <a href="/wiki/Exxon_Valdez_oil_spill" title="Exxon Valdez oil spill">Exxon Valdez oil spill</a> resulted in the discharge of approximately 11 million US gallons (42,000 m<sup>3</sup>) of oil into <a href="/wiki/Prince_William_Sound" title="Prince William Sound">Prince William Sound</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-EVOSTC_FAQ_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EVOSTC_FAQ-176">[176]</a></sup> oiling 1,300 miles (2,100 km) of the remote Alaskan coastline. The Valdez spill is 36th worst <a href="/wiki/Oil_spill" title="Oil spill">oil spill</a> in history in terms of sheer volume.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>The State of Alaska's Exxon Valdez Oil Spill Trustee Council stated that the spill "is widely considered the number one spill worldwide in terms of damage to the environment".<sup id="cite_ref-EVOSTC_FAQ_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EVOSTC_FAQ-176">[176]</a></sup> Carcasses were found of over 35,000 birds and 1,000 sea otters. Because carcasses typically sink to the seafloor, it is estimated the death toll may be 250,000 <a href="/wiki/Seabirds" class="mw-redirect" title="Seabirds">seabirds</a>, 2,800 <a href="/wiki/Sea_otters" class="mw-redirect" title="Sea otters">sea otters</a>, 300 <a href="/wiki/Harbor_seals" class="mw-redirect" title="Harbor seals">harbor seals</a>, 250 <a href="/wiki/Bald_eagles" class="mw-redirect" title="Bald eagles">bald eagles</a>, and up to 22 <a href="/wiki/Killer_whales" class="mw-redirect" title="Killer whales">killer whales</a>. Billions of <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">salmon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Herring#Life_cycle" title="Herring">herring eggs</a> were also killed.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> It had a devastating effect on the local <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Native" class="mw-redirect" title="Alaska Native">Alaska Native</a> populations, many of which had for centuries relied largely on fishing to survive.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p><p>As of 2001, oil remained on or under more than half the sound's beaches, according to a 2001 federal survey. The government-created Exxon Valdez Oil Spill Trustee Council concluded that the oil disappears at less than 4 percent per year, adding that the oil will "take decades and possibly centuries to disappear entirely". Of the 27 species monitored by the council, 17 have not recovered. While the salmon population has rebounded, and the orca whales are recovering, the herring population and fishing industry have not.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p><p>Exxon was widely criticized for its slow response to cleaning up the disaster. John Devens, the Mayor of Valdez, has said his community felt betrayed by Exxon's inadequate response to the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Exxon later removed the name "Exxon" from its tanker shipping subsidiary, which it renamed "<a href="/wiki/SeaRiver_Maritime" title="SeaRiver Maritime">SeaRiver Maritime</a>". The renamed subsidiary, though wholly Exxon-controlled, has a separate corporate charter and board of directors, and the former <i><a href="/wiki/Exxon_Valdez" title="Exxon Valdez">Exxon Valdez</a></i> is now the <i>SeaRiver Mediterranean</i>. The renamed tanker is legally owned by a small, stand-alone company, which would have minimal ability to pay out on claims in the event of a further accident.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></p><p>After a trial, a jury ordered Exxon to pay $5 billion in punitive damages, though an appeals court reduced that amount by half. Exxon appealed further, and on June 25, 2008, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Supreme Court">United States Supreme Court</a> lowered the amount to $500 million.<sup id="cite_ref-supreme_appeal_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-supreme_appeal-184">[184]</a></sup></p><p>In 2009, Exxon still uses more single-hull tankers than the rest of the largest ten oil companies combined, including the Valdez's sister ship, the SeaRiver Long Beach.<sup id="cite_ref-Nightingale_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nightingale-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Exxon.27s_Brooklyn_oil_spill"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Exxon's_Brooklyn_oil_spill">Exxon's Brooklyn oil spill</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Exxon's Brooklyn oil spill" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Greenpoint_oil_spill" title="Greenpoint oil spill">Greenpoint oil spill</a></div>
<p>New York Attorney General <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Cuomo" title="Andrew Cuomo">Andrew Cuomo</a> announced on July 17, 2007 that he had filed suit against the Exxon Mobil Corp. and ExxonMobil Refining and Supply Co. to force cleanup of the oil spill at Greenpoint, Brooklyn, and to restore <a href="/wiki/Newtown_Creek" title="Newtown Creek">Newtown Creek</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cuomo_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cuomo-186">[186]</a></sup></p><p>A study of the spill released by the <a href="/wiki/US_Environmental_Protection_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="US Environmental Protection Agency">US Environmental Protection Agency</a> in September 2007 reported<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> that the spill consists of 17 to 30 million US gallons (64,000 to 114,000 m<sup>3</sup>) of petroleum products from the mid-19th century to the mid-20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> The largest portion of these operations were by ExxonMobil or its predecessors. By comparison, the Exxon Valdez oil spill was approximately 11 million US gallons (42,000 m<sup>3</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-EVOSTC_FAQ_176-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EVOSTC_FAQ-176">[176]</a></sup>  The study reported that in the early 20th century <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil_of_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Oil of New York">Standard Oil of New York</a> operated a major refinery in the area where the spill is located. The refinery produced fuel oils, gasoline, kerosene and solvents. <a href="/wiki/Naptha" class="mw-redirect" title="Naptha">Naptha</a> and gas oil, secondary products, were also stored in the refinery area. Standard Oil of New York later became Mobil, a predecessor to Exxon/Mobil.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Baton_Rouge_Refinery_pipeline_oil_spill">Baton Rouge Refinery pipeline oil spill</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Baton Rouge Refinery pipeline oil spill" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In April 2012, a crude oil pipeline, from the Exxon Corp Baton Rouge Refinery, burst and spilled at least 1,900 barrels of oil (80,000 gallons) in the rivers of Point Coupee Parish, Louisiana, shutting down the Exxon Corp Baton Refinery for a few days. Regulators opened an investigation in response to the pipeline oil spill.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters-April-2012_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-April-2012-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Baton_Rouge_Refinery_benzene_leak">Baton Rouge Refinery benzene leak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Baton Rouge Refinery benzene leak" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On June 14, 2012, a bleeder plug on a tank in the <a href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge_Refinery" title="Baton Rouge Refinery">Baton Rouge Refinery</a> failed and began leaking <a href="/wiki/Naphtha" title="Naphtha">naphtha</a>, a substance that is composed of many chemicals including <a href="/wiki/Benzene" title="Benzene">benzene</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> ExxonMobil originally reported to the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Department_of_Environmental_Quality" title="Louisiana Department of Environmental Quality">Louisiana Department of Environmental Quality</a> (LDEQ) that 1,364 pounds of material had been leaked.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>On June 18, Baton Rouge refinery representatives told the LDEQ that ExxonMobil's chemical team determined that the June 14 spill was actually a level 2 incident classification which means that a significant response to the leak was required.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-192">[192]</a></sup> On the day of the spill the refinery did not report that their estimate of spilled materials was significantly different from what was originally reported to the department. Because the spill estimate and the actual amount of chemicals spilled varied drastically, the LDEQ launched an in-depth investigation on June 16 to determine the actual amounts of chemicals spilled as well as to find out what information the refinery knew and when they knew it.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-193">[193]</a></sup>   On June 20, ExxonMobil sent an official notification to the LDEQ saying that the leak had actually released 28,688 pounds of benzene, 10,882 pounds of toluene, 1,100 pounds of cyclohexane, 1,564 pounds of hexane and 12,605 pounds of additional <a href="/wiki/Volatile_organic_compound" title="Volatile organic compound">volatile organic compound</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_192-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-192">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-193">[193]</a></sup> After the spill, people living in neighboring communities reported adverse health impacts such as severe headaches and respiratory difficulties.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-194">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:602px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ExxonMobil_Baton_Rouge.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/ExxonMobil_Baton_Rouge.jpg/600px-ExxonMobil_Baton_Rouge.jpg" decoding="async" width="600" height="131" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2853" data-file-height="621"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 600px;height: 131px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/ExxonMobil_Baton_Rouge.jpg/600px-ExxonMobil_Baton_Rouge.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="600" data-height="131" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ExxonMobil_Baton_Rouge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>ExxonMobil refinery in <a href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge" class="mw-redirect" title="Baton Rouge">Baton Rouge</a></div></div></div></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Yellowstone_River_oil_spill">Yellowstone River oil spill</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Yellowstone River oil spill" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a href="/wiki/File:YellowstoneRiverMap.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/YellowstoneRiverMap.jpg/290px-YellowstoneRiverMap.jpg" decoding="async" width="290" height="263" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1066" data-file-height="967"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 290px;height: 263px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/YellowstoneRiverMap.jpg/290px-YellowstoneRiverMap.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="290" data-height="263" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:YellowstoneRiverMap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Yellowstone River watershed</div></div></div>
<p>The July 2011 Yellowstone River oil spill was an oil spill from an ExxonMobil pipeline running from Silver Tip to <a href="/wiki/Billings,_Montana" title="Billings, Montana">Billings, Montana</a>, which ruptured about 10 miles west of Billings on July 1, 2011, at about 11:30 pm.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT-July-11_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-July-11-195">[195]</a></sup> The resulting spill leaked an estimated 1,500 barrels of oil into the <a href="/wiki/Yellowstone_River" title="Yellowstone River">Yellowstone River</a> for about 30 minutes before it was shut down, resulting in about $135 million in damages.<sup id="cite_ref-Pipelines_and_Hazardous_Materials_Safety_Administration_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pipelines_and_Hazardous_Materials_Safety_Administration-196">[196]</a></sup> As a precaution against a possible explosion, officials in <a href="/wiki/Laurel,_Montana" title="Laurel, Montana">Laurel, Montana</a> evacuated about 140 people on Saturday (July 2) just after midnight, then allowed them to return at 4 am.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT-July-11_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-July-11-195">[195]</a></sup></p><p>A spokesman for ExxonMobil said that the oil is within 10 miles of the spill site. However, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Montana" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Governors of Montana">Montana Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Brian_Schweitzer" title="Brian Schweitzer">Brian Schweitzer</a> disputed the accuracy of that figure.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> The governor pledged that "The parties responsible will restore the Yellowstone River."<sup id="cite_ref-HS3-jul-11_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HS3-jul-11-198">[198]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Mayflower_oil_spill">Mayflower oil spill</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Mayflower oil spill" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2013_Mayflower_oil_spill" title="2013 Mayflower oil spill">2013 Mayflower oil spill</a></div>
<p>On March 29, 2013, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pegasus_Pipeline&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pegasus Pipeline (page does not exist)">Pegasus Pipeline</a>, owned by ExxonMobil and carrying Canadian <a href="/wiki/Wabasca_oil_field" title="Wabasca oil field">Wabasca</a> <a href="/wiki/Oil_sands" title="Oil sands">heavy crude</a>, ruptured in <a href="/wiki/Mayflower,_Arkansas" title="Mayflower, Arkansas">Mayflower, Arkansas</a>, releasing about 3,190 barrels (507 m<sup>3</sup>) of oil and forcing the evacuation of 22 homes.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters120815_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters120815-199">[199]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> The Environmental Protection Agency has classified the leak as a <i>major spill</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup>  In 2015, ExxonMobil settled charges that it violated the federal Clean Water Act and state environmental laws, for $5.07 million, including $4.19 million in civil penalties. It did not admit liability.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters120815_199-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters120815-199">[199]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
